It will be seriously awesome, but if you'd like to do that now for only a few bucks, it's called Google Cardboard. And having spent the last couple of hours running the Cardboard app on my Moto X phone, I can tell you that it's a remarkable experience.<br><br>Yes, Google has published the instructions for making your own viewer from a couple of dollars worth of parts. But the I AM CARDBOARD kit was ready to assemble and took me only about a minute to fold where indicated, stick a few tabs into slots, and voil&agrave; - it was ready to nestle my phone inside and run the Cardboard app. There are several demos, including:<br>* Tutorial - A brief tutorial showing how to use Cardboard.<br>* Tour Guide  - The Versailles Palace in France, look around the grounds from a fixed location, then go inside.<br>* Exhibit - Museum exhibits, with real 3-dimensional views.<br>* Windy Day - An animated story with a cartoon mouse.<br>* Google Earth - Randomly selected scenes from around the planet; if you're feeling adventurous, you can fly!<br>* You Tube - A new way to view YouTube selections.<br>* Photo Sphere - Uses the Google Camera app.<br>* Street Vue - Please, don't ever drive this fast!<br><br>I started using the Cardboard app while sitting down, but you need to be able to look all around you, so sitting in a swivel chair helps. You can also stand, but my wife and I both got a touch of vertigo doing that. By the way, if you wear glasses and they won't fit in the viewer, you can cut off the outside wings of the viewer (it won't hurt the viewer, they're just there to block out stray light).</span><span class="a-declarative" data-action="columnbalancing-showfullreview" data-columnbalancing-showfullreview="{&quot;rest&quot;:&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Cardboard app is only compatible with certain smartphones at this time. Go to the Google Play Store and find the Cardboard app, and there&#39;s a link to a list of compatible phones. Cardboard has one big advantage over Occulus Rift. With the Occulus Rift viewer, you&#39;re physically tethered to a computer. With Cardboard, you&#39;re free as a bird. And you can even fly like one too! It&#39;s going to be even more fun as more Cardboard apps are developed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Anyway, back to the viewer. It&#39;s well made, and I assembled it in about one minute. There&#39;s one folded piece that has a strip of adhesive to hold it in place, but it sometimes popped loose, so I sealed it with a piece of tape, and it was fine. Eventually, I&#39;m sure that someone will make a viewer from more substantial materials, but the cardboard viewer looks to be pretty durable, and the only problem I&#39;m having with it is that my wife keeps taking it away to play with it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The product was provided to me for evaluation and review.&quot;}"><a class="a-link-normal" I'm for sure going to make my own headset next, but grab this one to experience it right the first time.  The NFC tag is cool, it is programmed to automatically load the stock cardboard app when you slide your phone onto the flap before you secure the velcro straps.  The magnet works very well, but I do have the google phone (Nexus 5).  Haven't tried it with other phones yet.  The chrome cardboard experiments website is a must to check out (The Bears swimming video was a big hit at work) as well as Tuscany Drive, Space TerrorVR & Flight VR Demo app.  All of these are a quick download with Google Play on my Nexus 5.  But back to this product, it's the one the Google Developers were given @ the Google Conference when this launched.  Beware of the cheaper boxes out there, they are either missing 1 or several of the following: NFC tag, magnet, or lenses.  I wrapped electrical tape around it and my head to make it hands free for the games with a controller.  Will DIY a head mount soon, but this was perfect to get a rich VR experience for cheap. </div>  </div>        <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="0" REVIEWER</span></a></span></span><span class="a-color-secondary"> on August 12, 2014</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-R1TWS6W6XDJ3BS" class="a-row a-spacing-small"><span class="a-size-mini a-color-secondary">Color Name: Box Color</span>      <div class="a-section">   Ever since I heard of Google Cardboard I was completely fascinated by this incredible simple device. Using just regular cardboard and a few simple off-the-shelf add-ons you can turn your ordinary Android phone into a very credible pair of virtual reality goggles. So I finally got a chance to play with one of these contraptions, and the experience has totally lived up to my expectations. There are quite a few virtual reality apps available right now on Google Play, and as long as you don't expect a top-level holodeck experience you will be really amazed. There are a couple of things to keep in mind though:<br><br>1. You should ideally have the latest generation or the one before it high-end Android phone. Something like Galaxy S4 or S5 for instance. I tried using it with Galaxy S3, and even though it worked, the experience was not as smooth as I would have liked and the app kept crashing.<br><br>2. Folding of this cardboard set is pretty straightforward, but it's not completely intuitive. What I mean by that is that there is really only one way to fold it, you don't need any tools to do it, but the exact 3D arrangement can be a bit tricky.<br><br>Overall I am really pleased with this little set. It's very well (for a piece of cardboard that is), and it can bring you a lot of fun. I certainly recommend it.<br><br>**** Product provided for review purposes. **** </div>  </div>        <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="0" For these reasons, I was ecstatic when Google released cardboard and I knew that I had to get one as soon as I could, and thus I landed myself with this product. When it arrived I was enthralled. I ripped open the cardboard and began the surprisingly easy construction. Once built I slipped my S5 in and was surrounded by the castle of Versailles. I couldn't believe the quality and the experience a simple piece of cardboard could give me until I tried this. Since the purchase, I have used it for computer games (streaming from my desktop), to view movies on a gigantic screen, and to coax a multitude of my co-workers into buying one for themselves.  So far everyone  I have had try this product has stood in awe as they look around to see themselves flying in Google earth or front and center for a youtube video.
